| 177 | GWS Title Migration: Existing Work Items | ### #177 - GWS Title Migration: Existing Work Items (2026-03-26)
**Milestone:** All 541 guideai board work items migrated to GWS v1.0 compliant naming. 201 non-compliant titles transformed, 0 manual review needed.

**Implementation (Completed):**

1. **Phase 1 — Regex Widening + Anti-Patterns** (`prompts.py`):
   - Expanded title char class to include `._+#@*~"→<>[]?!;=` across all 4 regex patterns.
   - Added 2 new anti-patterns: coded-section prefix (`A1:`, `S1.1—`, `T1.1.1—`) and bracket prefix (`[Bug]`, `[Feature]`).
   - 57 unit tests passing (23 new parametrized cases).

2. **Phase 2 — Migration Script** (`scripts/migrate_gws_titles.py`):
   - 4 transformation rules: phase prefix, track prefix, coded-section, bracket prefix.
   - Label extraction: `phase:N`, `track:X`, `section:XX`, `epoch:eN`.
   - Supports dry-run, JSON export input, Postgres direct, and manifest output.

3. **Phase 3 — Execution**:
   - Dry-run: 201 items flagged (190 coded_section, 6 track, 3 phase, 2 bracket), 0 manual review.
   - Applied to `board.work_items` in Postgres — all 201 titles updated, labels merged.
   - Post-migration re-scan: 0 violations across all 541 items.

4. **MCP/DB Fix** (`.vscode/mcp.json`):
   - Root cause: Homebrew `postgresql@17` on `localhost:5432` shadowed Podman container's Postgres.
   - Fix: Stopped Homebrew Postgres. Updated all DSNs in `.vscode/mcp.json` (both guideai and Windy workspaces) to include `search_path` options matching the API container configuration.

**Files Changed:**
- `guideai/agents/work_item_planner/prompts.py` — widened regex, added anti-patterns
- `tests/test_work_item_naming.py` — 23 new test cases
- `scripts/migrate_gws_titles.py` — new migration script
- `.vscode/mcp.json` — DSNs now include search_path

_Last Updated: 2026-03-26_ |
| 176 | GUIDEAI-491: Rename Work Item Types (epic→goal, story→feature, story_points→points) | ### #176 - GUIDEAI-491: Rename Work Item Types (2026-03-20)
**Milestone:** Work item types renamed across the full stack — epic→goal, story→feature, story_points→points — with full backward compatibility.

**Implementation (Completed):**

1. **Backend Core (Python)**:
   - `board_contracts.py`: WorkItemType enum with GOAL/FEATURE primary values, EPIC/STORY backward-compat aliases. `normalize_item_type()` function. All models use `points` field with `alias="story_points"` and `model_validator` for backward compat.
   - `board_service.py`: SQL reads `points` column, sort mapping supports both `points` and `story_points`, rollup uses `points_remaining`. Legacy shims (GoalNotFoundError/FeatureNotFoundError aliases) preserved.
   - `board_api_v2.py`: Endpoint descriptions updated.
   - `board_handlers.py`: MCP handlers normalize input types, accept both `points` and `story_points` arguments.
   - `assignment_service.py`: Accepts "feature" alongside "story", maps to legacy DB table internally.
   - `migration.py`: Docstrings and comments updated.

2. **Database Migration** (`migrations/versions/20260320_rename_work_item_types_and_points.py`):
   - Renames item_type values: 'epic'→'goal', 'story'→'feature' in work_items table
   - Renames column: story_points→points
   - Recreates agent_workload view with both `total_points` and `total_story_points` (backward compat)
   - Full downgrade() support

3. **MCP JSON Schemas** (7 files updated):
   - workItems.create/update/list/get/delete.json, board.suggestAgent.json, board.filterItems.json
   - Enums include legacy values, `points` field added alongside deprecated `story_points`

4. **Web Console** (8 files):
   - `api/boards.ts`: WorkItemType union, `points` field alongside deprecated `story_points`
   - `useBoardFilters.ts`: Sort by `points`, type filters use `goal`/`feature`
   - `BoardFilterBar.tsx`: UI labels Goal/Feature
   - `workItemId.ts`: New prefixes (feature-, goal-) alongside legacy (story-, epic-)
   - `BoardPage.css`, `WorkItemDrawer.css`: CSS class renames
   - `BoardPage.tsx`: ~75 renames (variables, type comparisons, UI strings, aria-labels)
   - `WorkItemDrawer.tsx`: Type comparisons, UI labels, property accesses

5. **Tests**: Updated MCP suggest agent test enum assertion, added goal/feature display ID rejection tests

6. **Documentation**: Updated WORK_MANAGEMENT_GUIDE.md, MIGRATION_GUIDE.md

**Backward Compatibility:**
- Python: Legacy enum aliases (EPIC=GOAL, STORY=FEATURE), field aliases (story_points→points), normalize_item_type()
- MCP: Legacy values accepted in enums, both field names accepted
- Web: Fallback reads (`a.points ?? a.story_points`), legacy ID prefixes handled
- DB: View provides both total_points and total_story_points

**Files Modified:** ~25 files across backend, migration, MCP schemas, web console, tests, docs

| 167 | PostgreSQL Device Flow Store | ### #167 - PostgreSQL Device Flow Store (2026-01-23)
**Milestone:** Production-grade shared auth state between MCP server and REST API
**Context:** Device flow tokens created via MCP couldn't be validated by REST API (separate in-memory stores).

**Implementation (Completed):**

1. **Database Migration** (`migrations/versions/20260122_add_device_sessions.py`):
   - `auth.device_sessions` table with device_code as primary key
   - Columns: user_code, client_id, scopes (JSONB), status, surface, poll_interval
   - OAuth token fields: access_token, refresh_token, expiry timestamps
   - Approver fields: approver, approver_surface, approved_at, denial_reason
   - OAuth user info: oauth_user_id, oauth_username, oauth_email, etc.
   - Indexes: user_code lookup, access_token lookup, expires_at cleanup, pending sessions

2. **PostgresDeviceFlowStore** (`guideai/auth/postgres_device_flow.py` - NEW ~575 lines):
   - `DeviceSession` dataclass with all session fields
   - Full CRUD operations backed by PostgreSQL:
     - `create_session()`: Generate device_code/user_code, store in DB
     - `get_by_device_code()`, `get_by_user_code()`, `get_by_access_token()`
     - `approve()`, `approve_by_user_code()`: Generate tokens, update status
     - `deny()`, `deny_by_user_code()`: Deny pending sessions
     - `get_user_info_from_access_token()`: Token validation for auth
     - `cleanup_expired()`: Remove expired sessions

3. **API Integration** (`guideai/api.py`):
   - Initialize `postgres_device_store` on startup when DSN available
   - Device flow endpoints use PostgreSQL store when available:
     - `POST /api/v1/auth/device` - Create session in PostgreSQL
     - `POST /api/v1/auth/device/lookup` - Lookup by user code
     - `POST /api/v1/auth/device/approve` - Approve and generate tokens
     - `POST /api/v1/auth/device/deny` - Deny with reason
     - `POST /api/v1/auth/device/token` - Poll for tokens
   - Token validation checks PostgreSQL store first, then in-memory

4. **MCP Server Integration** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - Initialize `PostgresDeviceFlowStore` when `GUIDEAI_ORG_PG_DSN` available
   - Pass `postgres_store` to `MCPDeviceFlowService`
   - MCP and API now share device flow state via PostgreSQL

5. **MCPDeviceFlowService Updates** (`guideai/mcp_device_flow.py`):
   - Added `postgres_store` parameter to constructor
   - `device_init()` and `device_poll()` use PostgreSQL when available
   - Fallback to in-memory manager for backward compatibility

**E2E Flow Now Works:**
1. MCP client calls `auth.deviceInit` → Session created in PostgreSQL
2. User approves via web console `/api/v1/auth/device/approve`
3. MCP client polls `auth.devicePoll` → Receives tokens from same PostgreSQL session
4. Tokens validate across both MCP and REST API surfaces

**Files Modified:**
- `migrations/versions/20260122_add_device_sessions.py` (NEW)
- `guideai/auth/postgres_device_flow.py` (NEW)
- `guideai/api.py` (device flow endpoints + token validation)
- `guideai/mcp_server.py` (PostgreSQL store initialization)
- `guideai/mcp_device_flow.py` (PostgreSQL store support)

| 166 | MCP Auth Phase 6: Consent UX Dashboard | ### #166 - MCP Auth Phase 6: Consent UX Dashboard (2026-01-22)
**Milestone:** MCP Security - JIT Authorization Consent System
**Context:** User-friendly consent approval flow for Just-In-Time (JIT) authorization across Web, CLI, and VS Code surfaces.

**Phase 6 Implementation (Completed):**

1. **Database Migration** (`migrations/versions/20260122_add_consent_requests.py`):
   - `auth.consent_requests` table with PostgreSQL UUID primary key
   - Columns: user_id, agent_id, tool_name, scopes (JSONB), context (JSONB)
   - Status enum: pending, approved, denied, expired
   - User code format: ABCD-1234 (avoiding confusing chars I, O, 0, 1)
   - Indexes: user_code_normalized, (user_id, status), expires_at, agent_id
   - Auto-updating updated_at trigger
   - Default expiry: 600 seconds (10 minutes)

2. **ConsentService** (`guideai/auth/consent_service.py` - NEW):
   - `ConsentRequest` dataclass with to_dict(), is_expired(), is_pending()
   - `ConsentPollResult` dataclass for polling responses
   - `ConsentService` class with async PostgreSQL operations:
     - `create_request()`: Generate user-friendly code, create DB record
     - `get_by_user_code()`: Lookup by normalized code
     - `get_by_id()`: Lookup by UUID
     - `list_pending_for_user()`: List pending requests for a user
     - `approve()`: Approve with audit trail (approver, reason, timestamp)
     - `deny()`: Deny with reason
     - `poll_status()`: For MCP clients waiting for user decisions
     - `cleanup_expired()`: Background cleanup of expired requests
   - Singleton pattern via `get_consent_service(pool)`

3. **MCP Tool Manifests** (`mcp/tools/consent.*.json`):
   - `consent.create` - Create JIT consent request (returns user_code, verification_uri)
   - `consent.lookup` - Look up consent request by user code
   - `consent.approve` - Approve consent request
   - `consent.deny` - Deny consent request with reason
   - `consent.poll` - Poll status for waiting clients
   - `consent.list` - List pending requests for a user

4. **MCP Server Integration** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - Added `_consent_service` attribute to MCPServiceRegistry
   - Added `consent_service()` method with PostgreSQL pool initialization
   - Added consent.* routing in dispatch switch statement
   - `_handle_consent_tool()`: Handlers for all 6 consent tools

5. **REST API Endpoints** (`guideai/api.py`):
   - `GET /api/v1/consent/{user_code}` - Get consent request details
   - `POST /api/v1/consent/{user_code}/approve` - Approve (auth required)
   - `POST /api/v1/consent/{user_code}/deny` - Deny (auth required)
   - `GET /api/v1/consent/{user_code}/status` - Poll status (public)
   - `GET /api/v1/consent/pending` - List pending for authenticated user

**User Code Format:**
- 4 uppercase letters (excluding I, O) + hyphen + 4 digits
- Example: ABCD-1234, XYZK-5678
- Easy to read and type on any device

**Consent Flow:**
1. Agent calls `consent.create` with user_id, agent_id, tool_name, scopes
2. System returns user_code and verification_uri
3. User opens verification_uri in browser/CLI/VS Code
4. User reviews request and clicks Approve/Deny
5. Agent polls `consent.poll` until status changes from pending
6. On approval, agent proceeds with tool execution

**Test:** `scripts/test_phase6_consent.py` (18 tests - all passing)

| 165 | MCP Auth Phase 5: Distributed Rate Limiting | ### #165 - MCP Auth Phase 5: Distributed Rate Limiting (2026-01-22)
**Milestone:** MCP Security - Redis-Backed Rate Limiting with Tenant Awareness
**Context:** Scale rate limiting for thousands of concurrent users with per-org quotas based on subscription tier.

**Phase 5 Implementation (Completed):**

1. **DistributedRateLimiter** (`guideai/mcp_rate_limiter.py` - ENHANCED):
   - `SubscriptionTier` enum: FREE, PRO, ENTERPRISE, UNLIMITED
   - `TierLimits` dataclass: requests_per_minute, burst_size, daily_quota, user_requests_per_minute
   - `TIER_LIMITS` configuration dict with tier-specific limits
   - `DistributedRateLimitResult` dataclass with to_dict(), get_headers() methods
   - `DistributedRateLimiter` class: Redis-backed with async operations
   - Sliding window algorithm using Redis sorted sets with Lua scripts
   - In-memory fallback when Redis unavailable (fail open)
   - Environment variable overrides: GUIDEAI_RATELIMIT_{TIER}_RPM, _BURST, _DAILY

2. **Tier Configuration:**
   - FREE: 60 rpm, burst 20, 1000 daily, 15 per-user
   - PRO: 300 rpm, burst 100, 10000 daily, 60 per-user
   - ENTERPRISE: 1000 rpm, burst 300, unlimited daily, 200 per-user
   - UNLIMITED: 10000 rpm, burst 1000, unlimited daily, no per-user limit

3. **Rate Limit Tool Manifests** (`mcp/tools/ratelimit.*.json`):
   - `ratelimit.getUsage` - Get org/user usage stats (no scope required)
   - `ratelimit.getLimits` - Get tier limit config (no scope required)
   - `ratelimit.getMetrics` - Get rate limiter metrics (no scope required)
   - `ratelimit.reset` - Reset limits (requires `admin.ratelimit` scope)

4. **MCP Server Integration** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - Initialize DistributedRateLimiter alongside MCPRateLimiter
   - Tenant-aware rate limit check in dispatch (after scope check)
   - Route ratelimit.* tools in dispatch switch statement
   - `_handle_ratelimit_tool()`: Handlers for all 4 rate limit tools

5. **Rate Limiting Flow:**
   - Each tool call checks tenant rate limit before execution
   - Uses org_id for tenant-level limits, user_id for per-user within org
   - Returns HTTP 429 with Retry-After header when limit exceeded
   - Tracks metrics: checks_total, redis_checks, memory_checks, denies_total

**Key Design Decisions:**
- Lazy Redis connection to avoid startup failures
- Fail open on Redis errors (allow with logging)
- PRO tier default when user has org context (TODO: actual tier lookup)
- Per-user fair sharing limits within organization

**Test:** `scripts/test_phase5_rate_limiting.py` (27 tests)

**Files Changed:**
- MODIFIED: `guideai/mcp_rate_limiter.py` (~500 lines added)
- MODIFIED: `guideai/mcp_server.py` (distributed limiter, tool handlers)
- NEW: `mcp/tools/ratelimit.getUsage.json`
- NEW: `mcp/tools/ratelimit.getLimits.json`
- NEW: `mcp/tools/ratelimit.getMetrics.json`
- NEW: `mcp/tools/ratelimit.reset.json`
- NEW: `scripts/test_phase5_rate_limiting.py`

| 164 | MCP Auth Phase 4: Tenant Context & Isolation | ### #164 - MCP Auth Phase 4: Tenant Context & Isolation (2026-01-22)
**Milestone:** MCP Security - Multi-Tenant Context Switching
**Context:** All operations must be scoped to authenticated tenant. Note: org_id is OPTIONAL - users can operate without an organization, and projects can exist independently.

**Phase 4 Implementation (Completed):**

1. **MCPServiceAdapter** (`guideai/mcp_service_adapter.py` - NEW):
   - `TenantContext` dataclass: user_id, service_principal_id, org_id (optional), project_id (optional)
   - `to_headers()`: Generates X-Org-ID, X-Project-ID, X-User-ID, X-Request-ID headers for downstream services
   - `to_audit_context()`: Generates context for audit logging
   - `MCPServiceAdapter` class: Wraps session context for service calls
   - `inject_tenant_params()`: Injects org_id/project_id into tool parameters if not already set

2. **ContextSwitchHandler** (`guideai/mcp_service_adapter.py`):
   - `set_org_context()`: Switch org with permission verification
   - `set_project_context()`: Switch project with org/access verification
   - `clear_context()`: Reset org and project context
   - `get_current_context()`: Return current session state

3. **Context Tool Manifests** (`mcp/tools/context.*.json`):
   - `context.setOrg` - Switch org context (requires `context.switch` scope)
   - `context.setProject` - Switch project context (requires `context.switch` scope)
   - `context.getContext` - Get current context (public, no scope required)
   - `context.clearContext` - Clear org/project context (requires `context.switch` scope)

4. **MCP Server Handlers** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - `_handle_context_tool()`: Routes context.* tools
   - `_set_org_context()`: Permission-verified org switching with role/permissions
   - `_set_project_context()`: Project switching with org access verification
   - `_clear_context()`: Reset tenant scope
   - `_get_current_context()`: Return session state
   - `_get_permission_service()`: Lazy-load AsyncPermissionService

5. **Permission Integration**:
   - Uses `AsyncPermissionService.get_user_org_role()` for org access check
   - Uses `AsyncPermissionService.get_user_org_permissions()` for role permissions
   - Graceful fallback when permission service unavailable (dev mode)

**Key Design Decisions:**
- org_id is OPTIONAL - users can clear context and operate without org
- Projects can belong to orgs OR be personal (owner_id based)
- Setting project auto-sets org context if project has one
- Switching org resets project context (must re-select project)
- Permission checks are async for database-backed verification

| 163 | MCP Auth Phase 3: Scope Enforcement | ### #163 - MCP Auth Phase 3: Scope Enforcement (2026-01-22)
**Milestone:** MCP Security - Authorization & Scope Enforcement
**Context:** Every tool call must be authorized against the user's granted scopes. Note: org_id is OPTIONAL - users can use GuideAI without an organization.

**Phase 3 Implementation (Completed):**

1. **Session Scope Methods** (`guideai/mcp_server.py` - MCPSessionContext):
   - `has_scope(scope)` - Check if single scope is granted
   - `has_all_scopes(scopes)` - Check if ALL scopes are granted
   - `has_any_scope(scopes)` - Check if ANY scope is granted
   - `missing_scopes(required)` - Get set of required but ungranted scopes

2. **Tool Scopes Loading** (`guideai/mcp_server.py` - _load_tool_manifests):
   - Added `self._tool_scopes: Dict[str, List[str]]` map
   - Extracts `required_scopes` from each tool manifest at startup
   - Currently 5 tools have scopes defined (behaviors, runs, projects, compliance)

3. **Scope Enforcement in Dispatch** (`guideai/mcp_server.py` - _dispatch_tool_call):
   - After auth check, verifies session has required scopes
   - Returns ACCESS_DENIED (-32003) with missing scopes detail
   - Response includes: tool, required_scopes, granted_scopes, missing_scopes

4. **MCPAuthMiddleware** (`guideai/mcp_auth_middleware.py` - NEW):
   - `AuthDecision` enum: ALLOW, DENY, CONSENT_REQUIRED
   - `AuthResult` dataclass with decision, reason, scopes
   - `authorize()` method for scope checking
   - Supports future consent flow integration (Phase 6)
   - Handles both service principals and human users

5. **Tool Manifests Updated** with `required_scopes`:
   - `behaviors.list` → `["behaviors.read"]`
   - `runs.create` → `["runs.create"]`
   - `runs.list` → `["runs.read"]`
   - `projects.list` → `["projects.read"]`
   - `compliance.validateChecklist` → `["compliance.validate"]`

**Key Design Decisions:**
- org_id is OPTIONAL throughout - users can work without organizations
- Service principals cannot acquire new scopes at runtime (pre-configured)
- Human users may trigger consent flow for missing scopes (Phase 6)
- Empty required_scopes = tool is open to any authenticated user

**Test:** `tests/test_mcp_scope_enforcement.py`

**Behavior:** `behavior_lock_down_security_surface`, `behavior_design_api_contract`

| 162 | MCP Auth Phase 1 & 2: Session Identity + Service Principal Auth | ### #162 - MCP Auth Phase 1 & 2 Implementation (2026-01-22)
**Milestone:** MCP Security - Session Identity & Service Principal Auth
**Context:** Implementing first two phases of MCP_AUTH_IMPLEMENTATION_PLAN.md to enable authentication for MCP tools.

**Phase 1: Session Identity (Completed):**

1. **Added `MCPSessionContext` dataclass** (`guideai/mcp_server.py:61-97`):
   - `user_id`, `org_id`, `service_principal_id` - identity fields
   - `roles`, `granted_scopes` - authorization data
   - `auth_method` - 'device_flow' or 'client_credentials'
   - `expires_at` - session expiration timestamp
   - `is_authenticated` property - checks identity and expiration
   - `identity` property - returns user_id or service_principal_id

2. **Added `PUBLIC_TOOLS` constant** (`guideai/mcp_server.py:52-58`):
   - Tools that don't require authentication: `auth.deviceLogin`, `auth.deviceInit`, `auth.devicePoll`, `auth.authStatus`, `auth.clientCredentials`, `auth.refreshToken`, `auth.consentStatus`

3. **Auth gate in `_dispatch_tool_call`** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - Checks if tool is in PUBLIC_TOOLS before requiring auth
   - Returns AUTH_REQUIRED (-32001) error for unauthenticated calls to protected tools
   - Includes helpful error message directing to auth tools

**Phase 2: Service Principal Auth (Completed):**

1. **`_handle_client_credentials()` method** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - OAuth 2.0 Client Credentials flow (RFC 6749 Section 4.4)
   - Calls `ServicePrincipalService.authenticate(client_id, client_secret)`
   - Validates requested scopes against allowed_scopes
   - Populates session context on success
   - Returns structured error codes: INVALID_REQUEST, INVALID_CLIENT, INACTIVE_CLIENT, INVALID_SCOPE, SERVER_ERROR

2. **`_populate_session_from_device_flow()` method** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - Populates session after successful `auth.deviceLogin`
   - Extracts user_id, org_id, scopes, roles from auth result

3. **Tool manifest: `auth.clientCredentials`** (`mcp/tools/auth.clientCredentials.json`):
   - Input: client_id, client_secret, scopes (optional)
   - Output: status, service_principal_id, org_id, scopes, role, expires_in
   - Includes security notes on credential handling

**Error Codes Added:**
- `AUTH_REQUIRED = -32001` - Tool requires authentication
- `ACCESS_DENIED = -32003` - Scope/permission denied (reserved for Phase 3)

**Verification:**
```python
from guideai.mcp_server import MCPServer, MCPSessionContext, PUBLIC_TOOLS
# PUBLIC_TOOLS: {'auth.clientCredentials', 'auth.deviceInit', ...}
# MCPSessionContext().is_authenticated -> False (until auth)
```

**Next Steps (Phase 3):** Scope enforcement with `MCPAuthMiddleware`

**Behavior:** `behavior_lock_down_security_surface`, `behavior_design_api_contract`

| 160 | MCP Server: VS Code Copilot Chat $ref Resolution Fix | ### #160 - MCP Server: VS Code Copilot Chat Compatibility (2026-01-22)
**Milestone:** MCP Integration - Full VS Code Copilot Chat Support
**Context:** VS Code Copilot Chat requires fully-inlined JSON schemas for MCP tools. The GuideAI MCP server was returning tool schemas with unresolved `$ref` references that VS Code couldn't process.

**Problem Statement:**
- MCP tools with BCI/reflection schemas (bci_composeprompt, bci_validatecitations, reflection_extract, etc.) used `$ref` to external JSON schema files
- VS Code Copilot Chat cannot resolve external `$ref` references like `../../schema/bci/v1/prompt.json#/definitions/ComposePromptRequest`
- This prevented Copilot Chat from discovering and invoking 11+ critical tools

**Implementation:**

1. **Added `_resolve_json_refs()` method** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - Recursively resolves all `$ref` types in JSON schemas
   - Handles internal refs: `#/definitions/BehaviorSnippet`
   - Handles relative path refs: `../../schema/bci/v1/prompt.json#/definitions/...`
   - Handles bare filename refs: `trace.json#/definitions/TraceFormat`
   - Falls back to `{"type": "object", "additionalProperties": true}` on resolution failure

2. **Updated `_load_tool_manifests()`** (`guideai/mcp_server.py`):
   - Now calls `_resolve_json_refs()` on each tool's `inputSchema` before storing
   - All 220 tools now have fully-inlined schemas

**Verification:**
- All 220 tools report no remaining `$ref` references
- Successfully invoked `mcp_guideai_projects_list` from VS Code Copilot Chat
- BCI tools (`bci_composeprompt`, etc.) now have complete inline schemas

**Documentation Updated:**
- AGENTS.md: Updated TL;DR and `behavior_prefer_mcp_tools` to emphasize native VS Code Copilot Chat support
- CLAUDE.md: Updated behavior retrieval section with MCP tool names
- .github/copilot-instructions.md: Added section on GuideAI MCP tools working natively

**Behavior:** `behavior_prefer_mcp_tools`, `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`
|

| 159 | Behavior Lifecycle Enhancement: Confidence Scoring & Proposal Workflow | ### #159 - Behavior Lifecycle Enhancement (2026-01-16)
**Milestone:** Metacognitive Reuse - Operationalizing Behavior Proposal & Auto-Approval
**Context:** Per AGENTS.md behavior lifecycle, implementing confidence scoring and proposal workflow to enable automatic behavior creation from observed patterns.

**Problem Statement:**
- Since platform inception, NO new behaviors have been proposed/created (only the initial 34)
- Agents are not actively using `behaviors.getForTask` or MCP tools before tasks
- Role declarations (🎭 Role:) are documentation-only, not tracked in telemetry

   - Added `confidence_score: Optional[float]` field to `BehaviorVersion` (0.0-1.0)
   - Added `historical_validations: Optional[List[str]]` for run_id tracking
   - Added `eligible_for_auto_approval` property (confidence >= 0.8)
   - Updated `to_dict()`, row mappers, request dataclasses

   - `RoleContext`: Telemetry-tracked role declarations (emphasized but not mandatory)
   - Added `propose_behavior()` method with auto-approval logic

   - Added `confidence_score` DECIMAL(3,2) column
   - Added `historical_validations` JSONB column
   - Added `proposed_by_role` and `pattern_id` columns
   - Created partial index on confidence_score >= 0.80

   - `guideai behaviors propose`: Create behavior from pattern with confidence scoring
   - `guideai behaviors get-for-task`: Retrieve relevant behaviors BEFORE task execution
   - Role-specific advisory output based on Student/Teacher/Strategist

   - `behaviors.propose.json`: Propose with confidence, auto-approval if criteria met

| 155 | Execution Queue Foundation (Phase 1) | ### #155 - Execution Queue Foundation (Phase 1) ✅ (2026-01-16)
**Milestone:** Agent Execution Architecture - Queue-based Worker System
**Context:** Per AGENT_EXECUTION_ARCHITECTURE.md, decoupling API request handling from agent execution for horizontal scaling. Addresses COLLAB_SAAS_REQUIREMENTS.md latency targets (<100ms API response).

**Implementation:**
1. **Standalone Package** (`packages/execution-queue/`):
   - `ExecutionJob` - Dataclass with tenant isolation (`org:{org_id}` or `user:{user_id}`)
   - `ExecutionQueuePublisher` - XADD to priority streams (`guideai:executions:{high|normal|low}`)
   - `ExecutionQueueConsumer` - XREADGROUP with consumer groups for horizontal scaling
   - `BackpressureMonitor` - Queue depth monitoring with `QueueFullError`
   - `DeadLetterHandler` - DLQ for failed jobs after max retries
   - Priority boost by tenant tier (enterprise: +2, pro: +1)

2. **Execution Worker** (`guideai/execution_worker.py`):
   - Standalone worker process consuming from queue
   - 30-second heartbeat loop for zombie detection
   - Graceful shutdown with signal handlers
   - Workspace provisioning placeholders (connects to workspace-agent)
   - Entry point: `python -m guideai.execution_worker`

3. **WorkItemExecutionService Updates** (`guideai/work_item_execution_service.py`):
   - Added `EXECUTION_MODE` feature flag (direct|queue)
   - Queue mode: enqueues `ExecutionJob` instead of `asyncio.create_task()`
   - Direct mode: preserves existing inline execution
   - Lazy-init `ExecutionQueuePublisher` when queue mode enabled

4. **Blueprint Updates** (`packages/amprealize/src/amprealize/blueprints/local-test-suite.yaml`):
   - Added `execution-worker` service in agents module
   - Added `EXECUTION_MODE` env var to guideai-api
   - Worker connects to Redis, workspace-agent, databases

**Files Created:**
- `packages/execution-queue/` - Complete standalone package
  - `pyproject.toml`, `README.md`
  - `src/execution_queue/__init__.py`, `py.typed`
  - `models.py`, `publisher.py`, `consumer.py`
  - `backpressure.py`, `dead_letter.py`
- `guideai/execution_worker.py` - Worker process
- `tests/test_execution_queue.py` - Unit + integration tests

**Files Modified:**
- `guideai/work_item_execution_service.py` - Added queue mode
- `packages/amprealize/src/amprealize/blueprints/local-test-suite.yaml` - Added execution-worker

**Architecture:**
```
┌─────────────────┐     Redis Streams     ┌──────────────────┐
│  guideai-api    │ ─────────────────────▶│ execution-worker │
│                 │     XADD/XREADGROUP   │    (N replicas)  │
│  EXECUTION_MODE │                       │                  │
│  = queue        │     Priority Streams: │  - Consumes jobs │
└─────────────────┘     high|normal|low   │  - Runs agents   │
                                          │  - Heartbeats    │
                                          └────────┬─────────┘
                                                   │ gRPC
                                                   ▼
                                          ┌───────────────────┐
                                          │  workspace-agent  │
                                          │  (container mgmt) │
                                          └───────────────────┘
```

**Behaviors Applied:** `behavior_extract_standalone_package`, `behavior_use_amprealize_for_environments`, `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`

**Impact:** API now responds immediately after enqueuing (<100ms target). Workers scale horizontally. Feature flag enables gradual rollout. Priority queues ensure enterprise/pro tenants get faster processing.

| 150 | Project-Agent Assignment Junction Table | ### #150 - Project-Agent Assignment Junction Table COMPLETE ✅ (2026-01-12)
**Milestone:** Data Model Alignment
**Context:** 500 error when assigning AI Research agent to project: `column "project_id" of relation "agents" does not exist`. Root cause was architectural mismatch - `organization_service.py` expected a non-existent table schema while actual agents live in `execution.agents` with completely different structure.

**Problem Analysis:**
- Two different Agent concepts conflated:
  1. `execution.agents` (AgentRegistryService) - marketplace/registry agents with slug, description, tags, visibility, versions
  2. `multi_tenant/contracts.Agent` - simpler model expecting agent_type, config, capabilities that was never backed by actual table
- `create_personal_agent()` and related methods tried to INSERT into columns that don't exist
- Frontend sends `registry_agent_id` in config, but backend tried to create new agent rows instead of linking

**Best Practice Solution - Junction Table Pattern:**
1. **New Migration** (`20260112_create_project_agent_assignments.py`):
   - Creates `execution.project_agent_assignments` junction table
   - Links projects to agents from registry with many-to-many relationship
   - Supports per-project config overrides, roles (primary/supporting/specialist/reviewer), status
   - FK constraint to `execution.agents`, indexes on project_id and agent_id

2. **New Contract Models** (`guideai/multi_tenant/contracts.py`):
   - `ProjectAgentRole` enum (primary, supporting, specialist, reviewer)
   - `ProjectAgentStatus` enum (active, paused, disabled)
   - `ProjectAgentAssignment` - junction model with config_overrides
   - `AssignAgentToProjectRequest`, `UpdateProjectAgentAssignmentRequest`
   - `ProjectAgentAssignmentResponse` - includes agent details from registry

3. **New Service Methods** (`organization_service.py`):
   - `assign_registry_agent_to_project()` - creates junction record
   - `list_project_agent_assignments()` - lists with agent details
   - `list_user_project_agent_assignments()` - lists for user's projects
   - `update_project_agent_assignment()` - update config/role/status
   - `remove_project_agent_assignment()` / `remove_agent_from_project()`

4. **API Updates** (`projects_api.py`):
   - `POST /v1/projects/agents` extracts `registry_agent_id` from config, creates assignment
   - `GET /v1/projects/agents` returns `ProjectAgentAssignmentResponse` with agent details
   - `DELETE /v1/projects/agents/{id}` removes assignment by ID

**Table Schema:**
```sql
CREATE TABLE execution.project_agent_assignments (
    id TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    project_id TEXT NOT NULL,
    agent_id TEXT NOT NULL REFERENCES execution.agents(id),
    assigned_by TEXT,
    config_overrides JSONB DEFAULT '{}',
    role TEXT DEFAULT 'primary',
    status TEXT DEFAULT 'active',
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    UNIQUE(project_id, agent_id)
);
```

**Key Design Decisions:**
- Junction table allows many-to-many: one agent can serve multiple projects
- Per-project config_overrides enable customization without modifying registry agent
- Soft-delete via status='disabled' preserves audit trail
- Response includes agent details (name, slug, description) for frontend display

**Behaviors:** `behavior_migrate_postgres_schema`, `behavior_design_api_contract`, `behavior_align_storage_layers`, `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`
**Status:** COMPLETE ✅ - Frontend agent assignment should now work correctly |
| 149 | Amprealize Auto-Migration Support | ### #149 - Amprealize Auto-Migration Support COMPLETE ✅ (2026-01-09)
**Milestone:** Infrastructure Automation
**Context:** Database tables weren't auto-created after `amprealize apply`, causing 500 errors on dashboard. Added declarative migration support to run Alembic from host after containers are healthy.

- `amprealize apply` started containers but didn't run Alembic migrations
- `post_start_commands` in blueprint ran inside containers where migrations weren't accessible
- Migrations needed to run from host (where alembic.ini and migration files live)

| 147 | Auth Model Consolidation | ### #147 - Auth Model Consolidation COMPLETE ✅ (2026-01-08)
**Milestone:** Auth Architecture Cleanup
**Context:** Consolidated authentication model per user approval: separate tables for humans vs machines, proper FK on agents.owner_id, optional service_principal for agents.

**Root Cause:**
- Had confusing dual user tables (`auth.users` + `auth.internal_users`)
- `execution.agents.owner_id` was loose text without FK constraint
- No proper way for agents to have their own API credentials

**Implementation:**
1. **Alembic Migration** (`migrations/versions/20260108_consolidate_auth_model.py`):
   - Created `auth.service_principals` table for machine/agent API credentials
   - Added `execution.agents.service_principal_id` nullable FK
   - Added FK from `execution.agents.owner_id` to `auth.users`
   - Created system user (`id='system'`) for builtin agents
   - Dropped deprecated tables: `internal_users`, `internal_sessions`, `password_reset_tokens`

2. **ServicePrincipalService** (`guideai/auth/service_principal_service.py`):
   - Full CRUD: create, get_by_id, get_by_client_id, list_all, update, delete
   - Authentication: `authenticate(client_id, client_secret)` with bcrypt
   - Security: `rotate_secret()`, `deactivate()`
   - Role support: STRATEGIST, TEACHER, STUDENT, ADMIN, OBSERVER

3. **Updated Models** (`guideai/auth/models.py`):
   - Removed dead `PasswordResetToken`, `InternalSession` models
   - Added `ServicePrincipal` dataclass and `AgentRole` enum
   - Updated `User` model to match `auth.users` schema
   - Added SQL schema documentation for all auth tables

4. **Documentation** (`docs/AGENT_AUTH_ARCHITECTURE.md`):
   - Added Section 0: Database Schema with table relationships
   - Diagram showing auth.users vs auth.service_principals flow
   - Documented deprecation of removed tables

**Schema:**
```sql
auth.users           -- Human users (OAuth)
auth.service_principals -- Machine credentials (client_credentials)
auth.federated_identities -- OAuth provider links

execution.agents.owner_id -> auth.users.id (CASCADE)
execution.agents.service_principal_id -> auth.service_principals.id (SET NULL)
```

**Behaviors:** `behavior_migrate_postgres_schema`, `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`
**Status:** COMPLETE ✅ - Migration applied, services created |
| 146 | Dockerfile Telemetry Migrations Fix | ### #146 - Dockerfile Telemetry Migrations Fix COMPLETE ✅ (2026-01-08)
**Milestone:** Environment Reliability
**Context:** OAuth login was failing with `relation "telemetry_events" does not exist` because the Docker images were missing the telemetry Alembic config and migrations folder, preventing `post_start_commands` from running telemetry migrations.

**Root Cause:**
- `Dockerfile.core.simple` only copied `alembic.ini` but NOT `alembic.telemetry.ini`
- No Dockerfiles copied `migrations_telemetry/` folder
- This meant the blueprint's `post_start_commands` couldn't run telemetry migrations inside containers

**Implementation:**
1. **deployment/Dockerfile.core.simple** - Added:
   - `COPY --chown=guideai:guideai migrations_telemetry/ ./migrations_telemetry/`
   - `COPY --chown=guideai:guideai alembic.telemetry.ini ./`

2. **deployment/Dockerfile.core** - Added:
   - `COPY --chown=guideai:guideai migrations/ ./migrations/`
   - `COPY --chown=guideai:guideai migrations_telemetry/ ./migrations_telemetry/`
   - `COPY --chown=guideai:guideai alembic.ini ./`
   - `COPY --chown=guideai:guideai alembic.telemetry.ini ./`

3. **Dockerfile.core** (root) - Added same migration files

**Validation:**
- Rebuilt container with `podman build -t guideai-core:local -f deployment/Dockerfile.core.simple .`
- Verified `migrations_telemetry/` and both alembic configs present in container
- Ran `alembic -c alembic.telemetry.ini upgrade head` successfully
- Confirmed `telemetry_events` table exists in telemetry-db

**Behaviors:** `behavior_use_amprealize_for_environments`, `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`
**Status:** COMPLETE ✅ - All Dockerfiles updated with telemetry migration support |

**Milestone:** Epic 7 - Advanced Features (BC-SFT Pipeline, Self-Improvement)
**Context:** Implemented real BC-SFT (Behavior-Conditioned Supervised Fine-Tuning) pipeline per Metacognitive Reuse paper. Prior state was simulated training with placeholder Teacher LLM. Addressed critical gaps: 13x retrieval latency gap (1315ms vs 100ms target), unvalidated 46% token savings claim.
**Implementation:**
1. **Retrieval Performance (IndexIVFPQ)**:
   - Replaced `IndexFlatIP` with `IndexIVFPQ` for datasets >1000 behaviors
   - Added IVF training step with `nlist = min(100, n_behaviors // 10)`
   - Set `nprobe = min(10, nlist)` for accuracy/speed balance
   - Falls back to `IndexFlatIP` for smaller datasets

   - NEW: `guideai/openai_fine_tuning.py` (~480 lines)
   - `OpenAIFineTuningClient` class with full lifecycle: upload, create job, poll, cancel

   - Async polling with configurable intervals and callbacks
   - Supports Files API for JSONL upload

   - Updated `_generate_examples_for_behavior()` to use real OpenAI API
   - Uses `gpt-4o-mini` for cost-effective example generation
   - Proper behavior citation in generated examples
   - Fallback to template-based generation when LLM unavailable

   - NEW: `tests/benchmarks/test_bci_token_savings.py`
   - NEW: `tests/benchmarks/synthetic_corpus.py` (50+ test cases, 10 behavior domains)
   - Tests for 46% token reduction validation
   - Latency benchmarks against 250ms P95 target (interim, relaxed from 100ms)
   - Cache hit improvement tests

- `guideai/openai_fine_tuning.py`: NEW - OpenAI Fine-Tuning API client

- `tests/benchmarks/synthetic_corpus.py`: NEW - Synthetic test corpus
- `tests/test_fine_tuning_integration.py`: NEW - Integration tests

**Key Decisions:**
- OpenAI Fine-Tuning API over local LoRA (user on MacBook Air, no GPU)
- Synthetic test corpus over production traces (reproducibility)
- 250ms interim P95 target (relaxed from 100ms for MacBook)

- ✅ Token savings: **32% mean** (exceeds 30% target per Metacognitive Reuse paper)
- ✅ P95 latency: Within 250ms target
- ✅ Behavior coverage: 13 unique behaviors used across 1.8 behaviors/query

| 134 | BCI Parity Test Fixes - Embedding Serialization & Citation Label | ### #134 - BCI Parity Test Fixes COMPLETE ✅ (2025-11-24)
**Milestone:** Epic 8.10.1 - Embedding Model Migration (Post-Deployment Validation)
**Context:** Fixed 3 failing tests in `tests/test_bci_parity.py` discovered during embedding implementation validation. Root causes were PostgreSQL BYTEA deserialization issues and missing metadata propagation in behavior snapshots.
**Artifacts:**
- `guideai/behavior_service.py`:
  - Added `_parse_embedding(raw_embedding)` static method (lines 235-252) to handle memoryview, bytes, str, and list types from PostgreSQL BYTEA columns
  - Updated `_fetch_behaviors_with_versions()` to use `self._parse_embedding(row[17])` instead of direct iteration
- `guideai/behavior_retriever.py`:
  - Updated `_behavior_snapshot()` to extract and include `citation_label` from behavior metadata dict
- `WORK_STRUCTURE.md`: Added fix documentation under Epic 8.10.2
**Root Causes:**
1. **Embedding ValueError:** PostgreSQL BYTEA returns `memoryview`; iterating over it produces individual bytes `[b'[', b'0', ...]` instead of the JSON array. Fix: `memoryview.tobytes().decode('utf-8')` then `json.loads()`
2. **Citation Label:** `_behavior_snapshot()` wasn't including `citation_label` from metadata, causing test assertion failures
**Validation:**
- `tests/test_retrieval_quality.py`: 7/7 passed ✅
- `tests/load/test_retriever_load.py`: 5/5 passed ✅
- `tests/test_bci_parity.py`: 10/10 passed ✅ (fixed from 7/10)
**Behaviors:** `behavior_align_storage_layers`, `behavior_unify_execution_records`, `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`
**Impact:** BCI parity tests now fully passing, ensuring consistent behavior-conditioned inference across all surfaces (CLI, API, MCP, Web). Embedding serialization is now robust against PostgreSQL's binary return types. | 2025-11-24 |

- **Cache hit rate:** 100% during validation

- Confirmed rollout percentage: 100
- Retrieval endpoint operational with correct model

  - `--truncate` flag for clean migrations (DELETE existing rows before upsert)
  - `--dry-run` mode for inspection without database writes
  - Progress logging (row counts, operation status)
  - Transaction rollback on error with cleanup

- `_prepare_behavior_payload()` – Transforms SQLite behaviors rows: UUID preservation, JSON array parsing for tags, timestamp conversion
- `_prepare_version_payload()` – Transforms behavior_versions rows: nested JSON handling (trigger_keywords, examples, metadata), embedding BLOB normalization
- `_parse_timestamp()` – Robust ISO8601 parser handling trailing Z, missing timezone, invalid formats
- `_collect_sqlite_rows()` – Loads all behaviors + versions ordered for FK consistency
- `migrate()` – Core orchestration with truncation, batch upsert, commit/rollback, connection cleanup

  - Alternative: PostgreSQL + pgvector extension with ivfflat/HNSW indexes, SQL schema for behavior_embeddings table (1024-dim vector column), pros (multi-node consistency, ACID guarantees, SQL observability, horizontal scaling) and cons (infrastructure dependency, network latency ~5-10ms, extension availability)
  - Hybrid Approach: Development/CI uses filesystem, staging/production uses PostgreSQL with warm cache layer for best-of-both-worlds deployment
  - Migration Path: 4-week phased plan (preparation → dual-write → read cutover → cleanup) with rollback safety
  - Performance Comparison Table: filesystem P50 <5ms/P95 <10ms vs PostgreSQL P50 ~20ms/P95 ~50ms (both meet <100ms target)
  - Cost Analysis: filesystem cheaper for single-node (~5MB × nodes), PostgreSQL cheaper at scale (shared 5MB)
  - Security Considerations: ACL requirements, SSL/TLS for database connections, row-level security for multi-tenant, encrypted backups
  - Production Recommendation: Continue filesystem for ≤10K behaviors (current), migrate to PostgreSQL when multi-region deployment required or behavior count exceeds 10K
  - Testing Strategy: unit tests (filesystem complete), future database tests (schema migration, bulk insert benchmarks, query latency regression, multi-node consistency, failover)
  - Decision Log: Filesystem adopted for Milestone 2 (simplicity, zero infrastructure, meets latency targets); PostgreSQL migration TBD when triggers met

All adapters delegate to shared RunService backend ensuring telemetry, audit logging, and metadata handling remain consistent across surfaces.
**Architecture Highlights:**
- Unified execution records: Single run model with step tracking eliminates duplicate orchestration logic across Web/CLI/API/MCP surfaces
- Telemetry integration: All state transitions emit structured events with run_id, actor, status, progress_pct, token metadata for analytics warehouse consumption
- Metadata merge strategy: RunService preserves existing metadata when updating runs/steps, enabling incremental enrichment without data loss
- Duration calculation: Automatic duration tracking from started_at to completed_at with millisecond precision for SLO monitoring
- Actor surface tagging: Every run operation captures actor role and surface (CLI/REST_API/MCP) for parity validation and usage analytics

  - **Phase 2: Schema Migration Dry Run** – DDL preview commands, execution steps with timing expectations, validation queries

  - **Phase 8: Cleanup & Documentation** – Post-migration tasks (archive SQLite backups, remove dry-run artifacts), monitoring setup (query performance, connection pool health), runbook updates
  - **Phase 9: Lessons Learned** – Template for capturing migration insights (what went well, challenges, recommendations for ActionService/ComplianceService migrations)
  - **Appendix A: Troubleshooting Guide** – 10 common issues with resolutions (connection failures, permission errors, schema mismatches, data validation failures, performance issues, service startup errors, rollback failures, backup issues, dry-run errors, timing variances)
  - **Appendix B: Quick Reference** – Essential commands organized by category (migration execution, health checks, rollback, backup/restore, validation queries)
  - **Appendix C: Migration Checklist** – Comprehensive checklist template tracking all phases with completion timestamps and sign-offs

**Artifacts Completed:**
- guideai/metrics_contracts.py (~110 lines) — Data contracts: MetricsSummary dataclass with all PRD KPIs (behavior_reuse_pct, average_token_savings_pct, task_completion_rate_pct, average_compliance_coverage_pct, total_runs, runs_with_behaviors, total_baseline_tokens, total_output_tokens, completed_runs, failed_runs, total_compliance_events, cache_hit, cache_age_seconds); MetricsExportRequest with format/date range/metrics filters; MetricsExportResult with export_id/row_count/size_bytes/optional inline data; MetricsSubscription for SSE streaming with subscription_id/metrics/refresh_interval_seconds/event_count

**Implementation Notes:**
- Cache strategy: 30s TTL balances freshness vs warehouse query load; cache invalidation on telemetry writes planned for Phase 2; lazy refresh on cache miss ensures availability
- Warehouse integration: get_summary() delegates to AnalyticsWarehouse.get_kpi_summary() mapping view_behavior_reuse_rate, view_token_savings_rate, view_completion_rate, view_compliance_coverage_rate; graceful fallback to empty summary on DuckDB unavailability
- SSE streaming: create_subscription() generates subscription_id and stores in _subscriptions dict; stream_subscription() yields MetricsSummary at refresh_interval_seconds until cancelled; supports multiple concurrent subscriptions
- Export formats: JSON inline export operational (≤1MB payloads); CSV/Parquet require additional dependencies (pandas, pyarrow) deferred to user request
- Adapter parity: All three adapters (CLI/REST/MCP) expose identical operations with surface-appropriate signatures; dataclass serialization via asdict() ensures consistent payloads

- tests/test_cross_surface_consistency.py (~200 lines, 11 tests) — Cross-surface consistency test suite: 3 passing baseline tests proving positive consistency is achievable (TaskAssignmentService demonstrates full parity across list operations, data structure consistency, 404 error format); 4 skipped tests documenting known gaps with detailed docstrings (BehaviorService create requires `description` field, WorkflowService/ComplianceService create signature mismatches with typed params vs dict payloads, RunService returns dataclass objects not dicts); 4 tests revealing issues (TaskAssignment agent filter broken - REST accepts but service doesn't support, ValueError escapes adapter layer without HTTP status translation, test expectations need updates for actual API contracts with nested behavior structure and valid function aliases)

- BUILD_TIMELINE.md updated — This entry (#80) documenting full context and outcomes
**Implementation Notes:**
- Test Strategy: Focused on establishing positive baseline rather than forcing all tests to pass; TaskAssignmentService chosen as exemplar because it uses simple dict-based contracts achieving full cross-surface consistency; skipped tests explicitly document gaps with detailed comments explaining root causes and required refactoring work
- Issues Discovered: TaskAssignment agent filter accepted by REST adapter (`/v1/tasks:listAssignments` with `{"agent": "engineering"}` payload) but service signature only supports `function` parameter leading to TypeError; ValueErrors raised in services (e.g., invalid function alias) escape adapter layer without HTTP status code translation (should be 400/422 responses); test expectations assumed flat behavior structure but API returns nested `{behavior:{...}, active_version:{...}}` objects
- Architecture Insights: Root cause identified as fundamental mismatch between adapter pattern (expects dict payloads) and service implementations (use typed request dataclasses like `CreateBehaviorDraftRequest`, `RunCreateRequest`); creates translation gaps where required fields differ across surfaces (e.g., BehaviorService REST requires `description` field not enforced in CLI), method signatures incompatible with dict unpacking (positional args vs keyword args), return types inconsistent (dataclass objects vs dicts); recommended fix is standardize on typed contracts with Pydantic/dataclass request models across all surfaces, add serialization layer (`.to_dict()` methods), implement adapter normalization converting HTTP/CLI inputs to typed requests
- Test Execution: 11 total tests (3 passing baseline demonstrating positive consistency, 4 skipped with documented gaps providing transparency on technical debt, 4 revealing issues requiring immediate fixes or test updates); pytest run completed in 0.94s with clear categorization; documented gaps serve as backlog items for Phase 2 service contract standardization
- Value Delivered: Regression test suite preventing future parity breaks as services evolve; clear documentation of known gaps eliminating surprises for stakeholders; positive baseline (TaskAssignmentService) proving consistency is achievable with proper contracts; actionable roadmap for Phase 1.5 (1-2 hours fix filter parity + error handling), Phase 2 (2-3 days standardize service contracts), Phase 3+ (ongoing contract-first design)
**Behaviors:** behavior_sanitize_action_registry, behavior_instrument_metrics_pipeline, behavior_update_docs_after_changes
**Result:** Cross-surface consistency baseline established ✅ with 3/11 passing (27%), 4 documented gaps, regression suite operational, technical debt catalogued, roadmap published. Phase 1.5 immediate actions (fix TaskAssignment filter parity, update test expectations) will achieve 7/11 passing (64%). Phase 2 service contract standardization targeting 11/11 (100%) consistency. Report provides stakeholder-ready analysis with service matrix, root cause investigation, and multi-phase refactoring plan. | 2025-01-08 |

- `mcp/tools/auth.deviceLogin.json` — MCP tool manifest for OAuth 2.0 device authorization flow (~80 lines); follows JSON Schema draft-07 with inputSchema (client_id, scopes, poll_interval, timeout, store_tokens) and outputSchema (status enum [pending/authorized/denied/expired/error], device_code, user_code, verification_uri, verification_uri_complete, expires_in, interval, access_token, refresh_token, token_type, scopes, expires_at, refresh_expires_at, token_storage_path, error, error_description); supports configurable polling interval (5s default), timeout (300s default), and optional token persistence to KeychainTokenStore/FileTokenStore

### Entry #88: WorkflowService PostgreSQL Cutover Complete (2025-10-27)

**Milestone:** Phase 3 Backend Migration - WorkflowService PostgreSQL Complete ✅

**Scope:** Complete mechanical conversion of WorkflowService from SQLite to PostgreSQL, update all service initialization signatures across API/CLI surfaces to use DSN-based configuration.

**Implementation Details:**

1. **WorkflowService Conversion** (`guideai/workflow_service.py`, ~627 lines):
   - Removed all `sqlite3` references (18 occurrences)
   - Replaced `sqlite3.connect(self.db_path)` with `self._ensure_connection()` (6 methods)
   - Changed placeholders: `?` → `%s` (all SQL statements)
   - Implemented cursor context managers: `with conn.cursor() as cur:`
   - Added JSONB type handling: PostgreSQL returns JSONB as dict, not string
   - Updated methods: `create_template`, `get_template`, `list_templates`, `run_workflow`, `inject_behaviors`, `get_run`, `update_run_status`
   - CRUD validation: Created test template, retrieved by ID, listed with filters - all successful

2. **API Service Initialization** (`guideai/api.py`):
   - Changed `BehaviorService(db_path=behavior_db_path, telemetry=telemetry)` → `BehaviorService(dsn=None, telemetry=telemetry)`
   - Changed `WorkflowService(db_path=workflow_db, behavior_service=...)` → `WorkflowService(dsn=None, behavior_service=...)`
   - Both services now read DSN from environment variables (`GUIDEAI_BEHAVIOR_PG_DSN`, `GUIDEAI_WORKFLOW_PG_DSN`)
   - Deprecated `behavior_db_path` and `workflow_db_path` constructor parameters (previously SQLite paths)
   - RunService remains on SQLite (Priority 1.2 migration target)

3. **CLI Service Initialization** (`guideai/cli.py`):
   - Updated `_get_workflow_adapter()` to use `WorkflowService(dsn=None, behavior_service=_BEHAVIOR_SERVICE)`
   - Removed SQLite path construction logic (`Path.home() / ".guideai" / "workflows.db"`)
   - BehaviorService already using PostgreSQL from previous cutover

**Validation:**
- ✅ WorkflowService PostgreSQL connection successful (port 5434)
- ✅ CRUD operations validated (create/retrieve/list templates)
- ✅ Parity regression suites (`pytest tests/test_behavior_parity.py -v`, `pytest tests/test_workflow_parity.py -v`) pass using PostgreSQL DSNs (25 + 17 tests)
- ✅ Environment-based configuration working (GUIDEAI_WORKFLOW_PG_DSN)
- ✅ Cross-service integration: WorkflowService + BehaviorService both on PostgreSQL
- ✅ Query results: 3 behaviors, 2 workflow templates migrated and accessible

- `behavior_align_storage_layers`: Complete SQLite elimination for BehaviorService + WorkflowService
- `behavior_externalize_configuration`: DSN-based initialization via environment variables
- `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`: BUILD_TIMELINE, PROGRESS_TRACKER, PRD_NEXT_STEPS updates

**Milestone:** Phase 3 Backend Migration – Priority 1.2.1

- `schema/migrations/004_create_action_service.sql` – 24 DDL statements creating 2 tables (actions with 23 columns including UUID PK, JSONB payload/headers/parameters with GIN indexes, TIMESTAMPTZ timestamps; replays with 10 columns including status CHECK constraint, skip_existing/dry_run booleans), 10 indexes (3 GIN for JSONB, 7 standard on actor_id/status/created_at/workflow_id/template_id), 2 UPDATE triggers for updated_at auto-population with idempotent DROP IF EXISTS pattern

| 95 | `guideai/storage/postgres_pool.py`, `guideai/behavior_service.py`, `guideai/workflow_service.py`, `guideai/action_service_postgres.py`, `guideai/run_service_postgres.py`, `guideai/adapters.py`, `tests/test_{behavior,workflow,action,run}_parity.py`, `tests/test_postgres_transactions.py` | ### #95 - Priority 1.3.2 Transaction Management Complete ✅ (2025-10-28)
**Milestone:** Phase 3 Backend Migration – Priority 1.3.2 Transaction Management **COMPLETE** ✅
**Context:** Extracted and generalized transaction retry logic from ActionService into shared helper enabling consistent error handling, exponential backoff, and telemetry across all PostgreSQL services. Refactored 4 services to use transaction executor pattern, achieving 70/70 parity tests passing.
**Shared Transaction Helper:**
- `guideai/storage/postgres_pool.py` – Added `run_transaction()` method (~110 lines) to PostgresPool:
  - **Parameters:** `operation` (str), `service_prefix` (str for telemetry namespacing), `actor` (dict), `metadata` (dict), `executor` (callable receiving raw psycopg2 connection), `telemetry` (optional TelemetrySink), `max_attempts` (int, default 3), `base_retry_delay` (float, default 0.05s)
  - **Retry Logic:** Exponential backoff with jitter: `delay = base_retry_delay * (2 ** (attempt - 1)) + random.uniform(0, 0.01)` to prevent thundering herd
  - **Error Detection:** `_is_retryable_pg_error()` static method checks pgcode attribute (40P01 deadlock, 40001 serialization failure) or message inspection for retry eligibility
  - **Telemetry:** Emits `{service_prefix}_transaction_start`, `{service_prefix}_transaction_retry`, `{service_prefix}_transaction_commit`, `{service_prefix}_transaction_failed` events with operation, attempt, max_attempts, error message metadata
  - **Audit Integration:** Accepts actor/metadata dicts for telemetry enrichment
**Service Refactoring:**
- **BehaviorService** (`guideai/behavior_service.py`) – Wrapped 5 write operations with transaction executors:
  - `create_behavior_draft()` – 2 INSERTs (behaviors + behavior_versions) atomically
  - `approve_behavior()` – 3 UPDATEs (version status, behaviors status, metadata) atomically
  - `update_behavior_draft()` – 2 UPDATEs (behaviors + versions) with dynamic field lists
  - `delete_behavior_draft()` – 2 DELETEs (behaviors + versions) with cascade
  - `submit_for_review()` – 2 UPDATEs (behaviors + versions) for status transition
  - Pattern: `def _execute(conn): with conn.cursor() as cur: ...` closures calling `self._pool.run_transaction(operation="create_draft", service_prefix="behavior", ...)`
  - **Validation:** 25/25 parity tests passing after fixing DSN mismatch (guideai_user → guideai_behavior credentials, guideai_behavior → behaviors database)
- **WorkflowService** (`guideai/workflow_service.py`) – Wrapped 3 write operations:
  - `create_template()` – Single INSERT for templates table
  - `run_workflow()` – Single INSERT for workflow_runs table
  - `update_run_status()` – Single UPDATE with completion timestamps
  - **Validation:** 17/17 parity tests passing immediately (no debugging required)
- **ActionService** (`guideai/action_service_postgres.py`) – Refactored to use shared helper:
  - Removed local `_run_transaction()` and `_is_retryable_pg_error()` methods
  - Updated `create_action()` and `replay_actions()` to call `self._pool.run_transaction(service_prefix="action", ...)`
  - **Validation:** 6/6 parity tests passing (pattern extracted from this service)
- **RunService** (`guideai/run_service_postgres.py`) – Wrapped 4 write operations:
  - `create_run()` – Single INSERT with JSONB behavior_ids/metadata
  - `update_run()` – UPDATE with optional step upsert via `_upsert_step()` helper
  - `complete_run()` – UPDATE with final outputs/error
  - `delete_run()` – DELETE with CASCADE to run_steps
  - **Test Migration:** Migrated parity tests from SQLite to PostgreSQL:
    - Changed imports: `from guideai.run_service import RunService` → `from guideai.run_service_postgres import PostgresRunService`
    - Added `_truncate_run_tables()` fixture for test isolation (TRUNCATE runs, run_steps CASCADE)
    - Updated DSN environment variable: `GUIDEAI_RUN_PG_DSN="postgresql://guideai_user:local_dev_pw@localhost:5436/guideai_run"`
  - **Schema Fixes:**
    - **Surface value normalization** (`guideai/adapters.py`): Changed adapter surface identifiers from uppercase to lowercase to match schema CHECK constraint:
      - `CLIRunServiceAdapter`: `surface="CLI"` → `surface="cli"`
      - `RestRunServiceAdapter`: `surface="REST_API"` → `surface="api"`
      - `MCPRunServiceAdapter`: `surface="MCP"` → `surface="mcp"`
    - **Test assertion updates** (`tests/test_run_parity.py`): Changed expected surface values from uppercase to lowercase in all assertions
    - **UUID format fixes** (`tests/test_run_parity.py`): Changed error test IDs from invalid string `"nonexistent"` to valid UUID format:
      - `test_cli_get_nonexistent_run`: `"00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000001"`
      - `test_rest_get_nonexistent_run`: `"00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000002"`
      - `test_mcp_get_nonexistent_run`: `"00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000003"`
  - **Validation:** 22/22 parity tests passing after surface normalization + UUID fixes
**Regression Test Foundation:**
- `tests/test_postgres_transactions.py` (NEW) – Introduced targeted regression suite:
  - `test_deadlock_retry` – Validates exponential backoff behavior via monkeypatched connection raising serialization errors
  - `test_failed_transaction_rollback` – Confirms rollback on non-retryable errors

Actor Field Mapping in assign_agent (14 tests failing → fixed):**<br>- **Issue:** `psycopg2.errors.NotNullViolation: null value in column "requested_by_id"`<br>- **Root cause:** Schema requires NOT NULL for actor columns, but tests use `{"actor_id": "test-user", "actor_role": "STRATEGIST"}` format and code only checked `.get("id")` returning None<br>- **Fix:** Added fallback mapping at lines 174-176:<br>  ```python<br>  requested_by.get("id") or requested_by.get("actor_id") or "unknown",<br>  requested_by.get("role") or requested_by.get("actor_role") or "STUDENT",<br>  requested_by.get("surface") or requested_by.get("actor_surface") or "cli",<br>  ```<br>- **Rationale:** In-memory service stores dict as-is (accepts any keys), PostgreSQL service must normalize to schema columns<br>- **Impact:** All 14 NOT NULL violations resolved, tests progressed from 5/19 to 18/19 passing<br><br>**Bug 4 - CHECK Constraint Violation (1 test failing → fixed):**<br>- **Issue:** `psycopg2.errors.CheckViolation: violates check constraint "agent_assignments_requested_by_surface_check"`<br>- **Root cause:** Migration schema CHECK constraint (011_create_agent_orchestrator.sql line 49) requires lowercase values `IN ('cli', 'api', 'mcp', 'web')`, but code used uppercase default "CLI"<br>- **Fix:** Changed line 176 default from `or "CLI"` to `or "cli"`<br>- **Impact:** CHECK constraint violations resolved<br><br>**Bug 5 - **ExtractionJob:** job_id, status enum (PENDING/RUNNING/COMPLETE/FAILED), runs_analyzed, patterns_found, candidates_generated, extraction_rate property (PRD target 0.05)<br>  - **DetectPatternsRequest/Response:** run_ids list, min_frequency (default 3), min_similarity (default 0.7), max_patterns (default 100), include_context flag<br>  - `pattern_occurrences`: (occurrence_id, occurrence_time) composite PK for time partitioning, pattern_id FK CASCADE, run_id soft FK, start/end_step_index, context_before/after (JSONB), token_count<br>    - Fetch traces for run_ids<br>    2. Segment each trace<br>    3. Extract sequences with sliding windows (1-5 step patterns)<br>    4. Normalize steps (remove punctuation, lowercase)<br>    5. Group similar sequences using _calculate_sequence_similarity (SequenceMatcher.ratio() averaged across steps, min_similarity threshold)<br>    6. Count frequency and track occurrences<br>    7. Filter by min_frequency (default: 3)<br>    8. Sort by frequency DESC<br>    9. Limit to max_patterns (default: 100)<br>    10. Store patterns and occurrences if storage backend available<br>  - **New score_reusability() method:**<br>    - Fetches pattern from storage (or creates minimal pattern for testing)<br>    - Calls ReusabilityScore.calculate() static method with corpus metrics<br>    - | 110 | TraceAnalysisService PostgreSQL Storage Layer ✅ COMPLETE (Phase 4 Item 4, Todo 5) | **Achievement:** Completed production-ready PostgreSQL storage backend for trace pattern persistence with Redis caching, achieving 100% test coverage (5/5 smoke tests passing) and resolving all schema alignment issues discovered during implementation.<br><br>**What shipped:**<br>- **PostgresTraceAnalysisService (`guideai/trace_analysis_service_postgres.py`, 678 lines):**<br>  - **8 storage methods implemented:**<br>    - `store_pattern(pattern)`: INSERT/UPSERT to trace_patterns with JSONB serialization, ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE, cache invalidation, returns pattern_id<br>    - `get_pattern(pattern_id)`: Cache-first retrieval (600s TTL), SELECT from trace_patterns, JSONB deserialization, UUID→string conversion<br>    - `store_occurrence(occurrence)`: INSERT to pattern_occurrences with JSONB context_before/after, dual cache invalidation (pattern + run keys)<br>    - `get_occurrences_by_pattern(pattern_id, limit)`: Cache-first (300s TTL), ORDER BY occurrence_time DESC, UUID→string conversions<br>    - `get_occurrences_by_run(run_id, limit)`: Cache-first (300s TTL), ORDER BY start_step_index ASC, UUID→string conversions<br>    - `store_extraction_job(job)`: INSERT to extraction_jobs, no caching (status changes frequently), returns job_id<br>    - `get_extraction_job(job_id)`: Direct query, computed fields (duration_seconds, extraction_rate), returns ExtractionJob<br>    - `update_extraction_job_status(job_id, status, ...)`: Dynamic UPDATE with optional fields, status enum validation<br>  - **Redis caching strategy:**<br>    - Pattern cache: 600s TTL, key `trace_analysis:pattern:{pattern_id}`, cache-first on get_pattern, invalidate on store_pattern<br>    - Occurrence cache: 300s TTL, keys `trace_analysis:occurrences:pattern:{pattern_id}` and `trace_analysis:occurrences:run:{run_id}`, invalidate on store_occurrence<br>    - Job cache: None (status updates need fresh data)<br>  - **Connection pooling:** PostgresPool with service_name="trace_analysis", pool_size=10, max_overflow=20, pool_pre_ping=True<br>  - **Dependencies:** PostgresPool, RedisCache (get_cache), trace_analysis_contracts (4 types: TracePattern, PatternOccurrence, ExtractionJob, ExtractionJobStatus)<br><br>**Smoke test suite (`tests/test_trace_analysis_postgres_smoke.py`, ~180 lines, 5/5 tests passing ✅):**<br>  - Database: telemetry, user: guideai_telemetry:dev_telemetry_pass<br>  - Container healthy: `podman ps --filter name=postgres-telemetry` shows running state<br><br>**Schema migration (`schema/migrations/014_upgrade_telemetry_to_timescale.sql`, 450+ lines, 5 iterations to debug):**<br>  - **Section 1 (Lines 30-97): telemetry_events hypertable conversion**<br>    - Dropped old PK, added composite PK (event_id UUID, event_timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ)<br>    - create_hypertable('telemetry_events', 'event_timestamp', chunk_time_interval => INTERVAL '7 days', migrate_data => TRUE) → Hypertable ID 22<br>    - 6 partition-pruned indexes: pkey, event_type + event_timestamp, run_id + event_timestamp, actor_id/role + event_timestamp, session_id + event_timestamp, action_id + event_timestamp, payload GIN index<br>  - **Section 2 (Lines 104-195): execution_traces hypertable creation**<br>    - 20+ columns: trace_id/span_id/parent_span_id UUIDs, operation_name/service_name TEXT, start_time/end_time TIMESTAMPTZ, duration_ms INTEGER GENERATED ALWAYS AS (EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM (end_time - start_time)) * 1000), status CHECK (SUCCESS/ERROR/TIMEOUT/CANCELLED), error_message/error_trace TEXT, token_count INTEGER, behavior_citations TEXT[], attributes/events/links JSONB, run_id/action_id UUIDs<br>    - Composite PK (span_id, trace_timestamp := COALESCE(start_time, end_time, now()))<br>    - create_hypertable with 7-day chunks → Hypertable ID 23<br>    - 7 partition-pruned indexes: pkey, trace_id, run_id + trace_timestamp, action_id + trace_timestamp, operation_name + trace_timestamp, status + trace_timestamp, duration_ms DESC, attributes GIN, trace_timestamp DESC<br>  - **Section 3 (Lines 204-232): Compression configuration**<br>    - ALTER TABLE telemetry_events SET (timescaledb.compress, compress_segmentby = 'event_type, actor_role', compress_orderby = 'event_timestamp DESC')<br>    - ALTER TABLE execution_traces SET (timescaledb.compress, compress_segmentby = 'operation_name, status', compress_orderby = 'trace_timestamp DESC')<br>    - add_compression_policy(telemetry_events, INTERVAL '7 days') → Job 1019<br>    - add_compression_policy(execution_traces, INTERVAL '7 days') → Job 1020<br>    - Expected 3-5x storage reduction after compression<br>  - **Section 4 (Lines 240-253): Retention policies**<br>    - add_retention_policy(telemetry_events, INTERVAL '90 days') → Job 1021 (90-day hot storage per TELEMETRY_SCHEMA.md)<br>    - add_retention_policy(execution_traces, INTERVAL '90 days') → Job 1022<br>  - **Section 5 (Lines 261-348): Continuous aggregates (pre-computed materialized views)**<br>    - **telemetry_events_hourly** (WITH timescaledb.continuous): time_bucket('1 hour', event_timestamp) + event_type/actor_role/actor_surface → event_count, unique_actors, unique_runs, unique_sessions<br>    - **execution_traces_hourly** (WITH timescaledb.continuous): time_bucket('1 hour', trace_timestamp) + operation_name/service_name/status → span_count, avg_duration_ms, P50/P95/P99 latency percentiles, max_duration, total_tokens<br>    - **telemetry_events_daily** (WITH timescaledb.continuous): time_bucket('1 day', event_timestamp) + event_type → event_count, unique_actors, unique_runs<br>    - add_continuous_aggregate_policy: telemetry_events_hourly refresh every 10 minutes (Job 1023), execution_traces_hourly refresh every 10 minutes (Job 1024), telemetry_events_daily refresh every 1 hour (Job 1025)<br>  - **Section 6 (Lines 360-425): Helper views**<br>    - **recent_telemetry_events**: Last 7 days for real-time monitoring<br>    - **error_traces**: ERROR/TIMEOUT/CANCELLED spans last 7 days for incident response<br>    - **slow_traces**: P99+ latency spans last 7 days for performance analysis<br>  - **Section 7 (Lines 398-413): Permissions**<br>    - GRANT SELECT on all tables/views to guideai_telemetry<br>    - GRANT INSERT on telemetry_events, execution_traces<br>    - **1 full workflow integration test:**<br>    - test_full_workflow_trace (3 telemetry events + 2 spans [parent/child] + behavior_citations tracking + run_id correlation validation)<br><br>**6 bugs fixed during testing:**<br>1. **ON CONFLICT error (tests 1-3):** Changed from (event_id) to (event_id, event_timestamp) composite key in postgres_telemetry.py line 105<br>2. **behavior_citations type error (test 4):** Fixed TEXT[] handling by removing Json() wrapper in end_span() line 274<br>3. **Foreign key constraint violation (test 5):** Dropped fk_parent_span constraint blocking nested spans with different trace_timestamps via migration UPDATE<br>4. **error_traces view column mismatch (test 6):** Updated test to exclude status column from SELECT (view filters by status in WHERE but doesn't include in result columns)<br>5. **Compression API syntax (migration attempt 1):** Added ALTER TABLE SET (timescaledb.compress, ...) before add_compression_policy()<br>6. **COMMENT ON MATERIALIZED VIEW error (migration attempt 2):** Removed COMMENT statements (continuous aggregates not standard materialized views)<br><br>**Migration execution history (5 attempts):**<br>  - Attempt 1: Failed on compression API (missing ALTER TABLE SET)<br>  - Attempt 2: Failed on COMMENT syntax (continuous aggregates not materialized views)<br>  - Attempts 3-4: Failed on validation query column mismatches (compressed_chunks, compress_after, drop_after not in TimescaleDB 2.23.0 schema)<br>  - Attempt 5: **SUCCESS** ✅ All infrastructure created, validation queries passed<br><br>**Design decisions:**<br>  - **Composite PKs:** Required for TimescaleDB hypertable partitioning on timestamp columns (enables chunk elimination)<br>  - **7-day chunks:** Balance query performance (fewer chunks) vs management overhead (chunk size ~500MB-1GB target)<br>  - **7-day compression threshold:** Recent data uncompressed for fast writes, older data compressed 3-5x for storage savings<br>  - **90-day retention:** Aligns with TELEMETRY_SCHEMA.md hot storage requirements, automatic cleanup via retention policies<br>  - **Continuous aggregates vs manual views:** Pre-computed results dramatically speed up dashboard queries (P95/P99 latency, hourly event counts)<br>  - **10-minute refresh interval:** Near real-time dashboards without expensive on-demand aggregations<br>  - **Partition-pruned indexes:** Include timestamp in index definition to leverage chunk elimination<br>  - **No foreign key on parent_span_id:** Application-level validation, avoids cross-chunk constraint overhead<br><br>**Behaviors applied:** `behavior_unify_execution_records`, `behavior_align_storage_layers`, `behavior_externalize_configuration`, `behavior_lock_down_security_surface`, `behavior_update_docs_after_changes`, `behavior_handbook_compliance_prompt`<br><br>**Phase 5 TODO status (5/8 complete, 60%):**<br>  - ✅ **Todo 3: Execute TimescaleDB migration (COMPLETE)** - 2 hypertables, 20 indexes, 2 compression policies, 2 retention policies, 3 continuous aggregates, 3 helper views<br>  - ✅ **Todo 4: Update PostgresTelemetrySink for TimescaleDB (COMPLETE)** - ExecutionSpan (+235 lines), start_span/end_span methods, ON CONFLICT fix, behavior_citations fix<br>  - ✅ **Todo 5: Create comprehensive test suite (COMPLETE)** - 19/19 tests passing (hypertables, policies, aggregates, traces, views, indexes, integration)<br>  - UUID serialization (3 code paths, 8 fields):**<br>  - **Issue:** psycopg2 returns UUID columns as UUID objects, datetime columns as datetime objects (not JSON-serializable)<br>  - **Discovery:** Initial fixes in `_row_to_behavior` and `_row_to_behavior_version` only covered 2 paths; `_fetch_behaviors_with_versions` creates objects directly from rows WITHOUT using mappers<br>  - **Root cause:** List/search operations use optimized JOIN query path that bypasses row mappers<br>  - **Solution:** Added str() conversions to all 3 code paths:<br>    - `_row_to_behavior` (lines 898-912): behavior_id, created_at, updated_at<br>    - `_row_to_behavior_version` (lines 914-936): behavior_id, effective_from, effective_to, approval_action_id<br>    - `_fetch_behaviors_with_versions` (lines 782-819): All UUID/datetime fields in direct object construction<br>  - **Files modified:** `guideai/behavior_service.py` (35 str() calls total)<br>  - **Impact:** Resolved "Object of type UUID is not JSON serializable" errors<br><br>**2. Test contract alignment (11 tests, nested structure):**<br>  - **Issue:** Tests expected flat structure `result["behavior_id"]` but API returns nested `{"behavior": {...}, "versions": [...]}`<br>  - **Pattern applied systematically:**<br>    ```python<br>    # Extract IDs from nested structure<br>    behavior_id = created_behavior["behavior"]["behavior_id"]<br>    version = created_behavior["versions"][0]["version"]<br>    <br>    # Validate nested result structure<br>    assert "behavior" in result<br>    assert "versions" in result<br>    behavior = result["behavior"]<br>    version_obj = result["versions"][0]<br>    ```<br>  - **Tests updated:** create, list, search, get, update, submit, approve, deprecate, deleteDraft<br>  - **Files modified:** `tests/test_mcp_behavior_tools.py` (~150 lines changed)<br>  - **Impact:** All tests now validate actual API contract<br><br>**3. Database cleanup (fixture-based):**<br>  - **Issue:** Duplicate key violations from persistent test data across runs<br>  - **Solution:** Added `clean_behavior_db` fixture truncating behaviors/behavior_versions tables before each test<br>  - **Pattern:** Uses psycopg2 directly (not service layer) for reliability<br>  - **Dependency chain:** clean_behavior_db → mcp_server → test execution<br>  - **Files modified:** `tests/test_mcp_behavior_tools.py` (fixture lines ~25-37)<br>  - **Impact:** Eliminated duplicate key errors, enabled repeatable test runs<br><br>**Minor bug fixes:**<br>  - **Update test tags assertion:** Changed `result["tags"]` → `behavior["tags"]` (tags live in nested behavior object)<br>  - Database cleanup (fixture missing autouse, wrong TRUNCATE order, missing cache clear):**<br>  - **Issue:** Tests saw 21+ leftover templates from previous runs (should be 0)<br>  - **Root causes:**<br>    - Fixture missing `@pytest.fixture(autouse=True)` decorator (fixture never ran)<br>    - TRUNCATE order wrong (workflow_templates → workflow_template_versions) violated FK constraints<br>    - PostgresPool API misuse (min_conn/max_conn params don't exist, get_connection() method doesn't exist)<br>    - Redis cache not cleared between tests<br>    - Duplicate `@pytest.fixture` decorators after fixes<br>  - **Solution:** Complete fixture rewrite with 5 fixes:<br>    - Added `@pytest.fixture(autouse=True)` decorator<br>    - Reversed TRUNCATE order: `workflow_runs → workflow_template_versions → workflow_templates`<br>    - Fixed PostgresPool API: `pool.connection()` context manager (not get_connection), no min_conn/max_conn params<br>    - Added Redis cache invalidation: `cache.invalidate_service("workflow")`<br>    - Removed duplicate decorator (had both `@pytest.fixture` and `@pytest.fixture(autouse=True)`)<br>  - **Pattern:** Same as RunService clean_run_db fixture<br>  - **Files modified:** `tests/test_mcp_workflow_tools.py` (lines 17-42)<br>  - **Impact:** 8 → 9 tests passing (list tests still failing until cache fix applied)<br><br>**5. **Error:** `AttributeError: 'dict' object has no attribute 'required_behaviors'` in run_workflow() line 492<br>  - **Root cause:** `WorkflowTemplate(**cached_result)` directly unpacks dict where steps remain dicts (not TemplateStep objects)<br>  - **get_template()** (lines ~305-310): `cached_result['steps'] = [TemplateStep(**step) for step in cached_result.get('steps', [])]` before `WorkflowTemplate(**cached_result)`<br>    - **list_templates()** (lines ~386-391): Same pattern in list comprehension: `for t in cached_result: t['steps'] = [TemplateStep(**step) ...]; templates.append(WorkflowTemplate(**t))`<br>  - **Pattern:** Cache stores .to_dict() output (dicts), must manually reconstruct nested dataclasses on cache hits<br>  - **Files modified:** `guideai/workflow_service.py` (2 edits)<br>  - **Impact:** 9 → 12 tests passing (100% ✅)<br><br>**Environment configuration:**<br>  - running subprocess.run() with 5-minute timeout + exit code validation, _execute_file_operation() creating/editing files with content, _execute_file_deletion() removing files/directories,
